The Impossibility of Influence: The Second Doubt
The author argues that influence is impossible both when the effect exists and when it does not, refuting an objection about instantaneous creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma that claims influence is impossible whether the effect exists or not, and how an objection about instantaneous creation is refuted.

Core Idea
Influence is impossible in both existence and non-existence — a classic kalam dilemma.

This passage presents a powerful argument against the very possibility of causal influence. The author sets up a dilemma: influence must occur either when the effect already exists or when it does not. Both options lead to logical dead ends, and even a proposed escape via instantaneous creation fails on closer inspection. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the argument's flow.
2
Map the two cases
List the two possible states (existence and non-existence) and the reason each is impossible.
3
Trace the objection and its refutation
Identify the objection about the 'first moment' and how the author shows it fails.
The refutation uses the same dilemma: at that first moment, either something proceeds or not.
4
Formulate the final conclusion
State the overall conclusion: the very notion of influence is logically impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية : إن تأثير المؤثر في الأثر إما أن يكون حال وجود الأثر ، أو حال عدمه والقسمان باطلان ، فكان القول بالتأثير باطلاً ، وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع يؤثر المؤثر في الأثر حال وجود الأثر : لامتناع إيجاد الموجود ، وتحصيل الحاصل. وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يؤثر في الأثر حال عدم الأثر لأن الأثر حال عدمه باقي كما كان ، وإذا بقي الأثر كما كان على العدم المحض ، والنفي الصرف ، فحينئذ لم يصدر عن هذا الشيء المسمى بالمؤثر ، أثر في هذا الوقت البتة

فثبت : أن الأثر ما دام يكون باقياً على عدمه ، فإن المؤثر يمتنع كونه مؤثراً فيه ، وإذا صار الأثر موجوداً ، فإنه يمتنع كون المؤثر مؤثراً فيه . وإذا كان لا واسطة بين كون الأثر معدوماً وبين كونه موجوداً ، وثبت أن القول بالتأثير ممتنع في كلتا الحالتين ، ثبت أن القول بأصل التأثير محال

ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال إنه في الآن الأول يجعله موجوداً في الآن الثاني ؟ لأنا نقول : إنه في الآن الأول ، هل صدر عنه أثر أم لا ؟ فإن لم يصدر عنه أثر البتة، كان حاله في الآن كما كان قبل ذلك ، وكما أنه قبل ذلك الآن ، صدق عليه أنه ما كان [ أثر ] مؤثراً في أثر . كذلك في هذا الآن ، وجب أن يصدق عليه أنه غير مؤثر فيه ، وأما إن صدر عنه في الآن الأول أثر ، فهو في ذلك الآن مؤثر لوجود ذلك الأثر ، وذلك الأثر موجود في ذلك الآن . فيعود الإلزام المذكور ، وهو أنه يلزم إيجاد الموجود ، وهو محال .
The second doubt: The influence of the cause upon the effect is either at the time of the effect's existence or at the time of its nonexistence. Both divisions are invalid, so the statement of influence is invalid. We only say: It is impossible for the cause to influence the effect at the time of the effect's existence because of the impossibility of producing the existent and obtaining the obtained. And we only say: It is impossible for it to influence the effect at the time of the effect's nonexistence because the effect in its state of nonexistence remains as it was, and if the effect remains as it was upon pure nonexistence and absolute negation, then nothing called 'influence' has proceeded from this thing called 'cause' at this time at all.

It is established: That as long as the effect remains upon its nonexistence, the cause is impossible to be a cause in it. And when the effect becomes existent, the cause is impossible to be a cause in it. And since there is no intermediary between the effect being nonexistent and being existent, and it is established that the statement of influence is impossible in both states, it is established that the statement of influence in principle is impossible.

And it cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that at the first moment it makes it existent in the second moment? Because we say: At the first moment, did an effect proceed from it or not? If no effect proceeded at all, its state in that moment is as it was before, and just as before that moment it was true that it was not a cause in an effect, likewise in this moment it must be true that it is not a cause in it. And if an effect proceeded from it in the first moment, then in that moment it is a cause for the existence of that effect, and that effect is existent in that moment. So the aforementioned problem returns, which is that it necessitates producing the existent, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the second shubha, which attempts to prove that the very notion of a cause influencing an effect is impossible. The argument is a dilemma: The cause's influence either occurs when the effect already exists or when it does not exist. If during existence, it would be producing what already exists, which is impossible (ījād al-mawjūd). If during non-existence, the effect is still non-existent, so no change occurs; the cause produces nothing. Both are impossible, so influence is impossible. The author then considers an objection: what if the cause creates the effect at the first moment to exist at the second moment (instantaneous creation over time)? The answer is that at that first moment, either something proceeds or not. If nothing proceeds, then the cause is ineffective. If something proceeds, then that effect exists at that first moment, so again producing the existent at that moment. Thus the objection fails, confirming the impossibility of influence.

Key Terms
تأثير (ta'thīr) - influence
حال وجود (ḥāl wujūd) - state of existence
حال عدم (ḥāl 'adam) - state of nonexistence
الآن الأول (al-ān al-awwal) - the first moment
إيجاد الموجود (ījād al-mawjūd) - producing the existent
تحصيل الحاصل (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil) - obtaining the obtained

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that influence can happen in a temporal sequence, e.g., cause acts at one moment to create effect later.
Correction: The argument shows that even if the cause acts at a first moment, the effect either exists at that moment (making it producing the existent) or does not (no influence), so the dilemma remains.

Checkpoint
What is the main flaw of the objection that a cause could make the effect existent at a later moment?
A) The cause would have to exist in two moments.
B) The first moment either produces an effect (which then exists at that moment) or not, so the problem remains.
C) Time is an illusion.
D) The effect cannot be created because it is contingent.

Key Takeaway
The second doubt argues that causal influence is logically impossible because it must occur either when the effect exists (producing the existent) or when it does not (no change), and even an attempted temporal escape fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in something, do you immediately attribute it to your own skill and effort, or do you pause to recognize that even your effort is created by God at every moment? This lesson argues that nothing besides God can truly produce an effect—how does that challenge the way you credit yourself?
?
Think of a time you felt frustrated because a 'cause' (like your hard work or a medical treatment) didn't produce the expected 'effect'. Did you assume the cause was supposed to work by itself? How might seeing every apparent cause as merely a context for God's direct action change your reaction to failure?
?
This lesson proves that causal influence is impossible both when the effect exists and when it doesn't. If you truly internalize that, what would change about your reliance on things like money, people, or natural processes? Are you ready to shift your trust entirely to the Creator of the effect—whether it comes or not?

The Third Shubha: Need is Not the Thing Itself (First Two Proofs)
The author presents the third shubha and two arguments that need cannot be the thing itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third shubha's dilemma and its first two arguments proving that need cannot be identical to the thing.

Core Idea
Need is a relation, not self; what is known is not what is unknown.

This passage presents the third doubt against the necessity of a cause. The skeptic argues that if a thing is said to be in need of a cause, then this need must be either identical to the thing or distinct. Both possibilities are argued to be false. The author begins to show why identity is impossible, listing three aspects, though only the first two are complete here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shubha's structure
Read the opening lines to see how the skeptic frames the dilemma: need is either identical or different, both invalid.
2
Study the first proof
The first aspect: one can conceive of the heavens and earth without knowing they need a cause; what is known and what is unknown are not identical.
This shows that need is not essential to the thing.
3
Study the second proof
The body is a self-subsistent essence, while need is a relation; relational attributes are not identical to the substance.
4
Note the incomplete third proof
The third aspect begins but is cut off. Consider that the argument is incomplete in this passage.
This is a text issue; the full argument may appear elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثالثة : لو صدق على الشيء كونه مفتقراً إلى المؤثر ومحتاجاً إليه ، لكان هذا الافتقار والاحتياج . إما أن يكون عن ذلك الشيء المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والاحتياج، وإما أن يكون مغايراً له . والقسمان باطلان فالقول بالافتقار والاحتياج باطل

أما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون نفس ذلك الشيء . فالوجوه : أحدها : إنه قد يعقل ذات السماء والأرض ، من يجهل [؟] كونها مفتقرين ومحتاجين إلى المؤثر ، والمحكوم عليه بكونه معلوماً ، ليس عين الشيء المحكوم عليه ، بكونه غير معلوم . وثانيها : إن الجسم ذات قائمة بالنفس غير مقول بالقياس إلى الغير ، والافتقار والاحتياج نسبة وماهيات مقولة بالقياس إلى الغير وذلك يوجب التغاير . وثالثها : إنا إذا قلنا : الجسم محتاج في وجوده إلى الغير ، كان
The third doubt: If it is true of a thing that it is in need (muftaqir) of a cause and in need (muḥtāj) of it, then this need (iftiqār) and need (iḥtiyāj) is either identical to that thing which is judged to be in need and need, or different from it. Both divisions are invalid, so the statement of need and need is invalid.

As for the explanation that it is impossible for it to be the thing itself: The aspects: One of them: Indeed, the essence of heaven and earth may be conceived by one who is ignorant of them being in need and needing a cause, and the thing judged to be known is not the same as the thing judged to be unknown. Second: Indeed, the body is a self-subsistent essence not predicated in relation to another, while need and need are a relation and quiddities predicated in relation to another, and that necessitates difference. Third: Indeed, when we say: The body needs in its existence the other, it was...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage introduces the third shubha, which targets the concept of need (iftiqār) itself. The argument is that if a thing is said to be in need of a cause, then this need is either the thing itself or something else. Both are claimed to be impossible, so the concept of need is invalid. The author then begins to prove that it cannot be the thing itself by listing three aspects. The first aspect: One can conceive of the heavens and earth without knowing they need a cause, and the known thing is not the same as the unknown thing. The second: The body is a self-subsistent essence not relative, while need is a relation, implying difference. The third aspect is incomplete, starting with 'When we say: the body needs in its existence the other...' where the text cuts off. Therefore the full argument is not available in this window.

Key Terms
افتقار (iftiqār)
احتياج (iḥtiyāj)
مغاير (mukhāyir)
نسبة (nisba)
ماهيات (māhiyyāt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that need is an intrinsic attribute of a thing, identical to its essence.
Correction: The passage argues that need is a relational attribute (nisba) distinct from the thing itself, as shown by the possibility of being unaware of it and by the contrast between self-subsistence and relation.

Checkpoint
According to the third shubha, what is one reason that need is not the same as the thing itself?
A) The thing is known while need is unknown.
B) The thing is self-subsistent while need is a relational attribute.
C) The thing is eternal while need is temporal.
D) The thing is caused while need is uncaused.

Key Takeaway
The first two arguments of the third shubha prove that need cannot be identical to the thing because need is a relational concept, distinct from the thing itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever treated your need for God as something fixed and automatic, rather than a living relationship that you must constantly acknowledge? This lesson forces you to see need not as an intrinsic part of you, but as a connection to your Creator. Will you begin today to consciously recognize your dependency in every moment?
?
The skeptic's goal is to remove the very concept of need from your understanding of existence. Is there an area of your life where you resist admitting your need for God—perhaps your intellect, your ability, or your relationships? Would you be willing to confess that need in that area right now?
?
You conceive of yourself as a self-subsisting person, but the second proof shows that your very existence is relational: you are in need of the Other. How does it change your self-image if you see your 'self' as fundamentally defined by its relation to the Necessary Being? Will you let that reshape how you live today?

4 min
Proof of the Impossibility of Influence (Ta'thir) and Refutation of a Counterargument
The author proves impossibility of influence using the two states of the effect and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the concept of causal influence (ta'thir) is considered impossible in kalam, and how the argument refutes a temporal objection.

Core Idea
Influence is impossible: either the effect doesn't exist or it already does – both lead to contradiction.

This lesson unpacks a key kalam argument against causal influence between the Creator and creation. The author presents a logical dichotomy: the effect is either non-existent or existent, and in both cases 'influence' leads to absurdity. Then he tackles a clever counterargument about moments of creation, showing it collapses upon analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the original argument
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Let the author's reasoning unfold without interruption.
Notice the tight logical structure.
2
Understand the two-case dichotomy
Identify how the author splits the state of the effect into two mutually exclusive cases: non-existent and existent. In both, he shows influence is impossible.
No third state exists.
3
Analyze the refutation of the objection
Read the objection about creation across moments. See how the author breaks the first moment into two sub-cases and shows each leads to contradiction.
The objection is turned back on itself.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider what this argument means for causality in kalam: if influence is impossible, then all causation is only from Allah directly, without intermediaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فثبت : أن الأثر ما دام يكون باقياً على عدمه ، فإن المؤثر يمتنع كونه مؤثراً فيه ، وإذا صار الأثر موجوداً ، فإنه يمتنع كون المؤثر مؤثراً فيه . وإذا كان لا واسطة بين كون الأثر معدوماً وبين كونه موجوداً ، وثبت أن القول بالتأثير ممتنع في كلتا الحالتين ، ثبت أن القول بأصل التأثير محال . ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال إنه في الآن الأول يجعله موجوداً في الآن الثاني ؟ لأنا نقول : إنه في الآن الأول ، هل صدر عنه أثر أم لا ؟ فإن لم يصدر عنه أثر البتة، كان حاله في الآن كما كان قبل ذلك ، وكما أنه قبل ذلك الآن ، صدق عليه أنه ما كان مؤثراً في أثر . كذلك في هذا الآن ، وجب أن يصدق عليه أنه غير مؤثر فيه ، وأما إن صدر عنه في الآن الأول أثر ، فهو في ذلك الآن مؤثر لوجود ذلك الأثر ، وذلك الأثر موجود في ذلك الآن . فيعود الإلزام المذكور ، وهو أنه يلزم إيجاد الموجود ، وهو محال .
So it is established: that as long as the effect remains in its non-existence, the influencer is prevented from being an influencer in it, and when the effect becomes existent, it is prevented from the influencer being an influencer in it. And since there is no intermediate between the effect being non-existent and it being existent, and it is established that the statement of influence is impossible in both states, it is established that the statement of influence itself is impossible. And it is not said: why is it not permissible to say that in the first moment He makes it existent in the second moment? For we say: in the first moment, did an effect issue from Him or not? If no effect issued from Him at all, His state in that moment was as it was before that, and just as before that moment it was true of Him that He was not an influencer on an effect, likewise in this moment it must be true of Him that He is not an influencer in it. And if an effect issued from Him in the first moment, then He is in that moment an influencer for the existence of that effect, and that effect is existent in that moment. So the aforementioned objection returns, namely that it necessitates the creation of what already exists, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the impossibility of causal influence (ta'thir) in the context of kalām arguments about the relationship between the Creator and creation. The author first establishes a dichotomy: the effect (athar) is either non-existent or existent, with no intermediate state. In both cases, the influencer (mu'aththir) cannot be said to be 'influencing' the effect. If the effect is non-existent, the influencer cannot affect something that does not exist. If the effect is existent, the influencer cannot affect something that already exists, as that would be a repetition (tahṣīl al-ḥāṣil). Therefore, the very concept of influence is impossible. The author then addresses a potential objection: could it be that in one moment the influencer makes the effect exist in the next moment? The author refutes this by examining both possibilities in the first moment: either no effect issues, in which case the influencer remains non-influential, or an effect does issue, in which case the effect already exists in that moment, again implying the impossible repetition. Thus the objection collapses.

Key Terms
أثر
مؤثر
تأثير
إيجاد الموجود
الآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Influence can happen across time, e.g., in the first moment the creator makes the effect exist in the second moment.
Correction: The argument shows that in any moment of supposed creation, the effect either does not exist (so no influence) or already exists (so repetition), thus influence is impossible even across time.

Checkpoint
Why does the author conclude that the statement of influence (ta'thir) is impossible?
A) Because the effect is never found.
B) Because in both states of the effect (non-existence and existence) influence leads to a contradiction.
C) Because influence requires a third thing.
D) Because the effect is self-sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The concept of causal influence (ta'thir) is impossible because in any state of the effect, whether non-existent or existent, 'influence' leads to logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in something, do you ever attribute it to your own skill or effort as if they had independent causal power? Can you, from this moment, consciously say 'Allah created this result directly' every time you notice a success?
?
Your heart feels attached to certain people or things as sources of comfort or provision. Will you now look at them as mere occasions for Allah's direct creation, and train your heart to depend on Him alone?
?
If every breath you take is directly created by Allah without any intermediate influence, then your next breath is a fresh act of creation. Does that make you feel His presence more intimately? What will you do today to remind yourself of that immediacy?

The Dichotomy and Impossibility of Need Being Identical
The author poses the third objection and proves need cannot be identical to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial argument that need (iftiqar) in a contingent being is either identical to its essence or separate, and the three proofs showing it cannot be identical.

Core Idea
Need cannot be the same as the thing itself; three reasons prove they are distinct.

This lesson begins the third objection by establishing a crucial dichotomy: the need that a thing has for its cause must be either the thing itself or something else. The author then provides three clear and specific arguments to show that identity is impossible, each appealing to conceptual, relational, and propositional evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and dichotomy
Read the Arabic passage that states the objection and the initial dichotomy. Notice how the author defines the two possibilities: need is either identical to the thing or separate.
The passage starts with 'الشبهة الثالثة' and ends with 'ويدل على المطلوب'.
2
Examine the first reason
The first reason: we can conceive the essence of heaven and earth without conceiving their need. This shows that the conception of need is not the same as the essence.
3
Examine the second reason
The second reason: body is a self-subsistent essence, while need is a relation. This difference necessitates that they are not identical.
Relation vs. self-subsistence is a key distinction.
4
Examine the third reason
The third reason: the proposition 'the body is in need' has a subject different from its predicate, unlike 'the body is a body'. This shows need is not identical.
If subject and predicate were identical, the proposition would be meaningless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثالثة : لو صدق على الشيء كونه مفتقراً إلى المؤثر ومحتاجاً إليه ، لكان هذا الافتقار والاحتياج . إما أن يكون عن ذلك الشيء المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والاحتياج، وإما أن يكون مغايراً له . والقسمان باطلان فالقول بالافتقار والاحتياج باطل . أما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون نفس ذلك الشيء . فالوجوه : أحدها : إنه قد يعقل ذات السماء والأرض ، من يجهل كونها مفتقرين ومحتاجين إلى المؤثر ، والمحكوم عليه بكونه معلوماً ، ليس عين الشيء المحكوم عليه ، بكونه غير معلوم . وثانيها : إن الجسم ذات قائمة بالنفس غير مقول بالقياس إلى الغير ، والافتقار والاحتياج نسبة وماهيات مقولة بالقياس إلى الغير وذلك يوجب التغاير . وثالثها : إنا إذا قلنا : الجسم محتاج في وجوده إلى الغير ، كان هذا الكلام قضية مفيدة ، وتشهد الفطرة بكون موضوعها مغايراً لمحمولها . وإن قلنا : الجسم جسم لم يكن كذلك ، وذلك يدل على المطلوب . وأما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون ذلك الاحتياج والافتقار أمراً مغايراً للذات ، فلان ذلك المغاير ، إما أن يكون مفهوماً عدمياً أو وجودياً . والقسمان باطلان . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونه عدمياً . فلانا إذا قلنا هذا الشيء لا يفتقر إلى الغير ، ولا يحتاج إليه ، كان صريح العقل حاكماً بأن هذا المفهوم سلبي ، وإذا كان نفي الافتقار والاحتياج مفهوماً عدمياً ، امتنع أن يكون ثبوت الافتقار والحاجة مفهوماً عدمياً، ضرورة أن أحد طرفي النقيض يجب أن يكون ثبوتياً ويكون الآخر عدمياً . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفهوم من الافتقار والاحتياج أمراً ثبوتياً فلوجهين : الأول : إنه لو كان أمراً ثبوتياً : لكان إما أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، أو ممكناً لذاته ، والأول باطل ، لأنه صفة للموجود الذي يكون ممكناً لذاته والصفة مفتقرة إلى الموصوف ، والمفتقر إلى الممكن أولى بالإمكان . والثاني أيضاً باطل ، لأن الاحتياج لما كان موجوداً ممكناً لذاته كان محتاجاً إلى الموجد ، فيكون حاجة الحاجة زائدة عليه ، ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . والثاني : إن الموصوف بهذا الافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد ، إما أن يكون موجوداً ، أو لا يكون ، فإن كان موجوداً كان الموجود موصوفاً بالافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد والمؤثر ، فيلزم تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال ، وإن كان معدوماً لزم اتصاف العدم المحض ، والنفي الصرف بالصفة الموجودة .
The third objection: If the description of something as being in need of the influencer and in need of it were true, then this need and requirement would either be from that thing itself which is judged to be in need and requirement, or it would be different from it. Both divisions are false, so the statement of need and requirement is false. As for the demonstration that it is impossible for it to be the same thing itself: the aspects are: First, that one may conceive the essence of the heaven and earth while being ignorant of their being in need and requiring the influencer, and what is judged as being known is not the same as what is judged as being unknown. Second, that the body is a self-subsisting essence not predicated in relation to another, while need and requirement are a relation and essences predicated in relation to another, and that necessitates their being different. Third, that when we say 'the body is in need of another in its existence', this statement is a meaningful proposition, and sound nature (fiṭra) testifies that its subject is different from its predicate. And if we say 'the body is a body' it is not so, and that indicates the desired conclusion. And as for the demonstration that it is impossible for that need and requirement to be something different from the essence: because that different thing is either a non-existent concept or an existent concept. Both divisions are false. We say: it is impossible for it to be non-existent because when we say 'this thing is not in need of another and does not need it', sound reason judges that this concept is negative. And if the negation of need and requirement is a non-existent concept, it is impossible for the affirmation of need and requirement to be a non-existent concept, of necessity one of the two opposites must be positive and the other non-existent. And we say: it is impossible for the concept of need and requirement to be a positive thing for two reasons: First: if it were a positive thing, it would either be necessary in itself or possible in itself. The first is false because it is an attribute of an existent that is possible in itself, and the attribute is in need of the described, and what is in need of something possible is more deserving of possibility. The second is also false because need, since it is an existent possible in itself, would need a bringer into existence, so the need of the need would be additional to it, and an infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. Second: the thing described by this need and requirement of the bringer into existence is either existent or not. If it is existent, then the existent would be described by need and requirement of the bringer and the influencer, necessitating the attainment of the attained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil), which is impossible. And if it is non-existent, it would necessitate describing pure non-existence and absolute negation with an existent attribute, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed argument against the reality of need (iftiqar) as a separate attribute of contingent beings. The author systematically refutes both possibilities: that need is identical to the essence, or that it is a separate attribute. The argument uses three reasons to show that need cannot be identical: (1) we can conceive of the essence without conceiving need; (2) body is self-subsistent while need is a relation; (3) the proposition 'body is in need' has a different subject and predicate, unlike 'body is body'. Then it argues that need cannot be a separate attribute: if it were a non-existent concept, its affirmation would contradict the nature of opposites; if it were an existent concept, it would be either necessary or impossible. Necessary is impossible because it is an attribute of a possible. Possible leads to infinite regress. Also, if the described is existent, need would be redundant; if non-existent, an attribute would inhere in nothing. Thus need is impossible.

Key Terms
افتقار
احتياج
مؤثر
ممكن لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that need is simply part of what a contingent thing is, like its essence.
Correction: The author shows that we can conceive the essence without conceiving need, and that the structure of language and reality distinguishes them.

Checkpoint
What is one reason the author gives to show that need (iftiqar) cannot be identical with the essence?
A) Because the essence is eternal.
B) Because the proposition 'body is in need' has a subject different from its predicate.
C) Because need is a substance.
D) Because need is known intuitively.

Key Takeaway
Need cannot be identical to the essence because we can conceive the essence without need, need is a relation while essence is not, and the proposition about need has a distinct subject and predicate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you truly acknowledge that your need for Allah is not just an idea but a real, defining relation? Or do you often live as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that every breath is dependent on Him? What one change in your daily routine would make you more conscious of your constant need?
?
The passage argues that need is not identical to the essence. Consider your own self: you know you are you, but do you ever confuse your temporary dependencies (health, wealth, relationships) with who you really are? How would your life look different if you separated your essence from your needs, trusting only in the One who is truly self-sufficient?
?
The third proof says that the statement 'the body is in need' is meaningful because subject and predicate differ. When you say 'I need Allah', does that statement truly reflect a real distinction between you and your need? Or have you said it so often it becomes a meaningless phrase? What would it take for that statement to be as real for you as 'I am alive'?

Proof That Need Cannot Be a Separate Non-Existent Concept
The author argues that need cannot be a separate non-existent attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why need (iftiqar) cannot be a separate non-existent (ʿadamī) attribute of contingent beings.

Core Idea
Affirmation of need cannot be a non-existent concept because opposites must differ in positivity.

Having shown that need is not identical to the essence, the author now considers the possibility that it might be a separate attribute. He first examines if it could be a non-existent (ʿadamī) concept—something like a privation. Through a careful analysis of the nature of opposites and negation, he demonstrates that such a notion is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument about non-existent concept
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'وأما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون ذلك الاحتياج والافتقار أمراً مغايراً للذات' up to 'ويكون الآخر عدمياً'. Identify the claim: need cannot be a non-existent concept.
This is a short but dense section.
2
Understand the logic of opposites
The author argues that if the negation of need is a non-existent concept (negative), then the affirmation of need must be positive. Because one of two opposites must be positive and the other negative.
Non-existent concept here means a privation or absence.
3
Apply to need
Since 'not needing' is clearly a negation (non-existent concept), 'needing' cannot also be a non-existent concept; it must be positive. Thus need cannot be a separate ʿadamī attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثالثة : لو صدق على الشيء كونه مفتقراً إلى المؤثر ومحتاجاً إليه ، لكان هذا الافتقار والاحتياج . إما أن يكون عن ذلك الشيء المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والاحتياج، وإما أن يكون مغايراً له . والقسمان باطلان فالقول بالافتقار والاحتياج باطل . أما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون نفس ذلك الشيء . فالوجوه : أحدها : إنه قد يعقل ذات السماء والأرض ، من يجهل كونها مفتقرين ومحتاجين إلى المؤثر ، والمحكوم عليه بكونه معلوماً ، ليس عين الشيء المحكوم عليه ، بكونه غير معلوم . وثانيها : إن الجسم ذات قائمة بالنفس غير مقول بالقياس إلى الغير ، والافتقار والاحتياج نسبة وماهيات مقولة بالقياس إلى الغير وذلك يوجب التغاير . وثالثها : إنا إذا قلنا : الجسم محتاج في وجوده إلى الغير ، كان هذا الكلام قضية مفيدة ، وتشهد الفطرة بكون موضوعها مغايراً لمحمولها . وإن قلنا : الجسم جسم لم يكن كذلك ، وذلك يدل على المطلوب . وأما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون ذلك الاحتياج والافتقار أمراً مغايراً للذات ، فلان ذلك المغاير ، إما أن يكون مفهوماً عدمياً أو وجودياً . والقسمان باطلان . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونه عدمياً . فلانا إذا قلنا هذا الشيء لا يفتقر إلى الغير ، ولا يحتاج إليه ، كان صريح العقل حاكماً بأن هذا المفهوم سلبي ، وإذا كان نفي الافتقار والاحتياج مفهوماً عدمياً ، امتنع أن يكون ثبوت الافتقار والحاجة مفهوماً عدمياً، ضرورة أن أحد طرفي النقيض يجب أن يكون ثبوتياً ويكون الآخر عدمياً . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفهوم من الافتقار والاحتياج أمراً ثبوتياً فلوجهين : الأول : إنه لو كان أمراً ثبوتياً : لكان إما أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، أو ممكناً لذاته ، والأول باطل ، لأنه صفة للموجود الذي يكون ممكناً لذاته والصفة مفتقرة إلى الموصوف ، والمفتقر إلى الممكن أولى بالإمكان . والثاني أيضاً باطل ، لأن الاحتياج لما كان موجوداً ممكناً لذاته كان محتاجاً إلى الموجد ، فيكون حاجة الحاجة زائدة عليه ، ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . والثاني : إن الموصوف بهذا الافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد ، إما أن يكون موجوداً ، أو لا يكون ، فإن كان موجوداً كان الموجود موصوفاً بالافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد والمؤثر ، فيلزم تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال ، وإن كان معدوماً لزم اتصاف العدم المحض ، والنفي الصرف بالصفة الموجودة .

Both divisions are false, so the statement of need and requirement is false. Third, that when we say 'the body is in need of another in its existence', this statement is a meaningful proposition, and sound nature (fiṭra) testifies that its subject is different from its predicate. And if we say 'the body is a body' it is not so, and that indicates the desired conclusion. And as for the demonstration that it is impossible for that need and requirement to be something different from the essence: because that different thing is either a non-existent concept or an existent concept. Both divisions are false. We say: it is impossible for it to be non-existent because when we say 'this thing is not in need of another and does not need it', sound reason judges that this concept is negative. And if the negation of need and requirement is a non-existent concept, it is impossible for the affirmation of need and requirement to be a non-existent concept, of necessity one of the two opposites must be positive and the other non-existent. And we say: it is impossible for the concept of need and requirement to be a positive thing for two reasons: First: if it were a positive thing, it would either be necessary in itself or possible in itself. The first is false because it is an attribute of an existent that is possible in itself, and the attribute is in need of the described, and what is in need of something possible is more deserving of possibility. The second is also false because need, since it is an existent possible in itself, would need a bringer into existence, so the need of the need would be additional to it, and an infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. Commentary
This passage presents a detailed argument against the reality of need (iftiqar) as a separate attribute of contingent beings. The author systematically refutes both possibilities: that need is identical to the essence, or that it is a separate attribute. The argument uses three reasons to show that need cannot be identical: (1) we can conceive of the essence without conceiving need; (2) body is self-subsistent while need is a relation; (3) the proposition 'body is in need' has a different subject and predicate, unlike 'body is body'. Then it argues that need cannot be a separate attribute: if it were a non-existent concept, its affirmation would contradict the nature of opposites; if it were an existent concept, it would be either necessary or impossible. Necessary is impossible because it is an attribute of a possible. Possible leads to infinite regress. Also, if the described is existent, need would be redundant; if non-existent, an attribute would inhere in nothing. Thus need is impossible.

Proof That Need Cannot Be a Separate Existent Concept
The author provides two reasons why need cannot be a separate positive attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments demonstrating that need (iftiqar) cannot be a separate existent (wujūdī) attribute.

Core Idea
If need were a separate existent, it would lead to either impossibility or infinite regress.

The final step of the objection: the author now proves that need cannot be a separate positive attribute. He presents two powerful arguments. The first argues that if need is positive, it must be either necessary or possible—both lead to absurdities. The second shows that the thing described by need is either existent or non-existent, and both cases are impossible. This completes the refutation of need as a real attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the existent concept
Read the Arabic passage from 'وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفهوم من الافتقار والاحتياج أمراً ثبوتياً' to the end. Identify the two reasons.
This is the longest part of the lesson.
2
Examine the first reason
If need is positive, it is either necessary or possible. Necessary is impossible because need is an attribute of a possible thing. Possible leads to an infinite regress of needs.
The first reason subdivides into two sub-arguments.
3
Examine the second reason
If the thing is existent, then need would be redundant (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil). If it is non-existent, an attribute cannot inhere in nothing.

الشبهة الثالثة : لو صدق على الشيء كونه مفتقراً إلى المؤثر ومحتاجاً إليه ، لكان هذا الافتقار والاحتياج . إما أن يكون عن ذلك الشيء المحكوم عليه بالافتقار والاحتياج، وإما أن يكون مغايراً له . والقسمان باطلان فالقول بالافتقار والاحتياج باطل . أما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون نفس ذلك الشيء . فالوجوه : أحدها : إنه قد يعقل ذات السماء والأرض ، من يجهل كونها مفتقرين ومحتاجين إلى المؤثر ، والمحكوم عليه بكونه معلوماً ، ليس عين الشيء المحكوم عليه ، بكونه غير معلوم . وثانيها : إن الجسم ذات قائمة بالنفس غير مقول بالقياس إلى الغير ، والافتقار والاحتياج نسبة وماهيات مقولة بالقياس إلى الغير وذلك يوجب التغاير . وثالثها : إنا إذا قلنا : الجسم محتاج في وجوده إلى الغير ، كان هذا الكلام قضية مفيدة ، وتشهد الفطرة بكون موضوعها مغايراً لمحمولها . وإن قلنا : الجسم جسم لم يكن كذلك ، وذلك يدل على المطلوب . وأما بيان أنه يمتنع أن يكون ذلك الاحتياج والافتقار أمراً مغايراً للذات ، فلان ذلك المغاير ، إما أن يكون مفهوماً عدمياً أو وجودياً . والقسمان باطلان . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونه عدمياً . فلانا إذا قلنا هذا الشيء لا يفتقر إلى الغير ، ولا يحتاج إليه ، كان صريح العقل حاكماً بأن هذا المفهوم سلبي ، وإذا كان نفي الافتقار والاحتياج مفهوماً عدمياً ، امتنع أن يكون ثبوت الافتقار والحاجة مفهوماً عدمياً، ضرورة أن أحد طرفي النقيض يجب أن يكون ثبوتياً ويكون الآخر عدمياً . وإنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفهوم من الافتقار والاحتياج أمراً ثبوتياً فلوجهين : الأول : إنه لو كان أمراً ثبوتياً : لكان إما أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، أو ممكناً لذاته ، والأول باطل ، لأنه صفة للموجود الذي يكون ممكناً لذاته والصفة مفتقرة إلى الموصوف ، والمفتقر إلى الممكن أولى بالإمكان . والثاني أيضاً باطل ، لأن الاحتياج لما كان موجوداً ممكناً لذاته كان محتاجاً إلى الموجد ، فيكون حاجة الحاجة زائدة عليه ، ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . والثاني : إن الموصوف بهذا الافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد ، إما أن يكون موجوداً ، أو لا يكون ، فإن كان موجوداً كان الموجود موصوفاً بالافتقار والاحتياج إلى الموجد والمؤثر ، فيلزم تحصيل الحاصل وهو محال ، وإن كان معدوماً لزم اتصاف العدم المحض ، والنفي الصرف بالصفة الموجودة .
The third objection: If the description of something as being in need of the influencer and in need of it were true, then this need and requirement would either be from that thing itself which is judged to be in need and requirement, or it would be different from it. Both divisions are false, so the statement of need and requirement is false. As for the demonstration that it is impossible for it to be the same thing itself: the aspects are: First, that one may conceive the essence of the heaven and earth while being ignorant of their being in need and requiring the influencer, and what is judged as being known is not the same as what is judged as being unknown. Second, that the body is a self-subsisting essence not predicated in relation to another, while need and requirement are a relation and essences predicated in relation to another, and that necessitates their being different. Third, that when we say 'the body is in need of another in its existence', this statement is a meaningful proposition, and sound nature (fiṭra) testifies that its subject is different from its predicate. And if we say 'the body is a body' it is not so, and that indicates the desired conclusion. And as for the demonstration that it is impossible for that need and requirement to be something different from the essence: because that different thing is either a non-existent concept or an existent concept. Both divisions are false. We say: it is impossible for it to be non-existent because when we say 'this thing is not in need of another and does not need it', sound reason judges that this concept is negative. And if the negation of need and requirement is a non-existent concept, it is impossible for the affirmation of need and requirement to be a non-existent concept, of necessity one of the two opposites must be positive and the other non-existent. And we say: it is impossible for the concept of need and requirement to be a positive thing for two reasons: First: if it were a positive thing, it would either be necessary in itself or possible in itself. The first is false because it is an attribute of an existent that is possible in itself, and the attribute is in need of the described, and what is in need of something possible is more deserving of possibility. The second is also false because need, since it is an existent possible in itself, would need a bringer into existence, so the need of the need would be additional to it, and an infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. Second: the thing described by this need and requirement of the bringer into existence is either existent or not. If it is existent, then the existent would be described by need and requirement of the bringer and the influencer, necessitating the attainment of the attained (taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil), which is impossible. And if it is non-existent, it would necessitate describing pure non-existence and absolute negation with an existent attribute, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed argument against the reality of need (iftiqar) as a separate attribute of contingent beings. The author systematically refutes both possibilities: that need is identical to the essence, or that it is a separate attribute. The argument uses three reasons to show that need cannot be identical: (1) we can conceive of the essence without conceiving need; (2) body is self-subsistent while need is a relation; (3) the proposition 'body is in need' has a different subject and predicate, unlike 'body is body'. Then it argues that need cannot be a separate attribute: if it were a non-existent concept, its affirmation would contradict the nature of opposites; if it were an existent concept, it would be either necessary or impossible. Necessary is impossible because it is an attribute of a possible. Possible leads to infinite regress. Also, if the described is existent, need would be redundant; if non-existent, an attribute would inhere in nothing. Thus need is impossible.

واجب لذاته
ممكن لذاته

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that need is a real positive attribute that can be added to a contingent thing.
Correction: The author shows that such a positive attribute leads to either impossibility (necessity in dependent) or infinite regress, or redundancy.

Key Takeaway

The Fourth Objection: Need and the Paradox of Priority and Posteriority
Razi refutes the fourth objection against causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the objection that need implies both priority and posteriority, thereby defending the logical necessity of a cause.

Core Idea
Need does not entail contradiction; the objection itself is impossible.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents and refutes a sophisticated objection against the principle of causality. The objection claims that if something needs a cause, it would have to be both prior and posterior to its need, which is absurd. Razi carefully dissects the reasoning and shows that the objection fails, thereby reaffirming the logical necessity of a cause for all contingent things.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection's structure
Read the opening statement of the objection. Notice that it claims need entails two contradictory relations: priority (as attribute) and posteriority (as effect). This sets up the paradox.
The objection is a reductio ad absurdum against the very idea of need.
2
Examine the two arguments for priority
Razi gives two reasons why need implies priority: first, need is an attribute so the thing is prior to it; second, need is a relation so the relata must exist before the relation. Understand each argument clearly.
These arguments rely on the principle that attributes and relations are ontologically dependent on their subjects.
3
Examine the argument for posteriority
The objector also argues that need implies posteriority: the thing needs the cause to bring it into existence, so the thing's existence must come after the cause's action, which is after the need. Therefore the thing is posterior to its own need.
This creates the contradiction: the same thing is both prior and posterior to its need.
4
Analyze the counter-objection and its answer
A potential response suggests distinguishing essence (prior) from existence (posterior). Razi refutes this by showing the essence either needs the cause (contradiction returns) or does not (then only existence needs it, but that also leads to contradiction).
This closes the loophole and completes the refutation.
5
Conclude the lesson
Reflect on how Razi's argument defends the necessity of a cause. The objection fails because it misidentifies the subject of need and conflates different senses of priority.
The lesson confirms that the need for a cause is logically coherent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الرابعة : لو صدق على شيء كونه مفتقراً إلى الموجد والمؤثر ، لزم كون تلك الماهية متقدمة بالرتبة على حصول هذه الحاجة ، وكونها متأخرة عن هذه الحاجة محال ، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوت الاحتياج : محال .
إنما قلنا : إنه يقتضي التقدم لوجهين :
الأول : إن افتقاره إلى المؤثر واحتياجه إليه صفة (٢) من صفاته ، وحكم من أحكامه ، وصريح العقل يقتضي بتقدم الموصوف على الصفة بالرتبة والثاني : إن افتقار الشيء واحتياجه إلى الغير، نسبة مخصوصة بينه وبين ذلك الغير ، وتحقق النسبة بين الشيئين يتوقف على تحقق الشيئين (٣) ، فوجب أن يكون الافتقار والاحتياج متأخرا بالرتبة عن تحقق الذات المحكوم عليها بالافتقار والاحتياج وإنما قلنا : إنه يقتضي التأخر ، وذلك لأن الافتقار إلى الفاعل إنما يحصل لأجل أن يجعله الفاعل متحققاً وحاصلاً وكائناً وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن يكون تحقق الأثر وتكونه متأخراً عن تأثير الفاعل فيه، لكن تأثير الفاعل فيه متأخر عن افتقاره واحتياجه إلى الفاعل ، والمتأخر عن المتأخر عن الشيء متأخر عنه فثبت : أن تحقق تلك الحقيقة المحكوم عليها بالافتقار والاحتياج إلى المؤثر يجب أن يكون متأخراً بالرتبة عن احتياجه إلى المؤثر ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أنه لو صدق على شيء كونه مفتقراً إلى المؤثر، ومحتاجاً إليه ، فإنه يلزم كون تلك الحقيقة متقدمة بالرتبة ، على حصول تلك الحاجة ، وكونها متأخرة عنه ، ومعلوم أن ذلك محال ، فوجب أن يكون القول بثبوت الاحتياج والافتقار باطلاً ومحالاً . ولا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال الموصوف بالافتقار والاحتياج الى المؤثر ، هو الماهية ، وهي متقدمة على حصول هذا الاحتياج والافتقار [ وأما الواقع بالفاعل والمؤثر فهو الوجود ، وهو متأخر بالرتبة عن حصول هذا الافتقار (١) ؟ لأنا نقول : الماهية من حيث هي هي، إما أن تكون مفتقرة الى المؤثر ، أو لا تكون ، فإن كانت مفتقرة إلى المؤثر لزم تقدمها على الافتقار وتأخرها عنه على ما بيناه ، فيعود الخلف، وإن لم تكن مفتقرة إلى المؤثرة، كان المفتقر إلى المؤثـر هـو الـوجـود فقط ، أو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود ، وعلى التقديرين فيلزم منه حصول التقدم والتأخر معاً وهو محال
The fourth objection: If it is true of something that it is dependent upon and in need of the originator and effector, then that essence would be prior in rank to the occurrence of this need, and its being posterior to this need is impossible. So it must be that maintaining the affirmation of need is impossible. We only said that it necessitates priority for two reasons: First: Its dependence on the effector and its need for it is an attribute from its attributes and a judgment from its judgments, and clear reason necessitates the priority of the described over the attribute in rank. Second: The dependence of a thing and its need for another is a specific relation between it and that other, and the realization of the relation between two things depends on the realization of the two things. So it must be that dependence and need are posterior in rank to the realization of the essence which is judged to have dependence and need. And we only said that it necessitates posteriority, because dependence on the agent only occurs so that the agent makes it realized, obtained, and existing. If so, then it must be that the realization and coming-to-be of the effect is posterior to the agent's effect in it. But the agent's effect in it is posterior to its dependence and need for the agent. And that which is posterior to that which is posterior to something is posterior to it. So it is established that the realization of that reality which is judged to have dependence and need for the effector must be posterior in rank to its need for the effector. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that if it is true of something that it is dependent upon the effector and in need of it, then it entails that reality being prior in rank to the occurrence of that need and being posterior to it. And it is known that this is impossible. So it must be that the statement affirming need and dependence is false and impossible. And let it not be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the thing described as having dependence and need for the effector is the essence, and it is prior to the occurrence of this need and dependence, while that which is produced by the agent and effector is existence, and it is posterior in rank to the occurrence of this dependence? For we say: The essence considered in itself either is dependent upon the effector or is not. If it is dependent upon the effector, then its priority over the dependence and its posteriority to it follows as we have explained, so the absurdity returns. And if it is not dependent upon the effector, then that which is dependent upon the effector is only existence, or the being-described of the essence by existence. In either case, it entails the occurrence of priority and posteriority together, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection (shubha) against the claim that things are in need of a cause, and then refutes it. The objection argues that if something is in need of a cause, then that thing would have to be both prior (in rank) to its need and posterior to it, which is contradictory. The author breaks down the reasoning: The need is an attribute of the thing, so the thing must be prior to its attribute (first reason). Also, the need is a relation between two things, so the relata must exist before the relation, making the need posterior to the thing (second reason). For posteriority: The need is for the cause to produce the thing, so the effect (the thing) must be posterior to the cause's action, but the cause's action is posterior to the thing's need for it, so the thing ends up posterior to its own need. Thus the thing would be both prior and posterior to its need, which is impossible. Therefore, the claim that things are in need of a cause is false. Then an objection is raised: Perhaps the essence (essence) is prior to the need, while the existence is posterior and is what actually needs the cause. The author responds: The essence either needs the cause or not. If it does, the same contradiction returns. If it does not, then only existence or the description of essence with existence is dependent, but in that case priority and posteriority still occur together, which is impossible. Thus the refutation holds.

احتياج
متقدم بالرتبة
متأخر بالرتبة
الماهية
الوجود
مؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objection is a valid criticism, showing that need is impossible.
Correction: The objection fails because it misidentifies the subject of need and conflates different senses of priority; Razi shows that the contradiction does not actually arise.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth objection, what logical consequence follows from saying something is in need of a cause?
A) The thing would be impossible.
B) The thing would be both prior and posterior to its need.
C) The thing would be eternal.
D) The cause would be unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
The objection that need implies contradictory priority and posteriority fails because it conflates different senses of priority and misidentifies the subject of need; Razi's refutation defends the coherence of causal dependence.

?
Razi shows that any attempt to separate essence from existence in causal dependence leads to contradiction. In your own life, do you ever try to claim a part of yourself that is 'yours' apart from God? What would it take to surrender that?
?
This objection is intellectually subtle, but at its core it denies that anything truly needs a Creator. Have you ever allowed intellectual pride to make you resistant to the simple truth that you are utterly dependent? What is the cost of that resistance in your relationship with Allah?

The Fifth Objection: Why the Dependent Cannot Be the Essence
Razi presents the fifth objection and begins refuting the first candidate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth objection against the need for a cause and the beginning of its refutation, focusing on why the essence itself cannot be the dependent entity.

Core Idea
The essence cannot depend on a cause because it cannot cease to be what it is.

Razi presents the fifth objection to the claim that things need a cause. He argues that the dependent entity cannot be the essence, existence, or the combination. He then begins to prove the first impossibility using two logical arguments. This lesson covers the objection and the initial refutation, though the full answer is incomplete in this passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection statement
Identify the three candidates Razi rules out as the dependent entity: essence, existence, and the being-described of essence by existence.
This sets up the need to prove four divisions, but only the first is covered here.
2
Study the first proof
The first proof uses the principle that if something is by another, it must cease when that other ceases. If essence were dependent, removal of cause would remove essence, but essence cannot cease to be itself (e.g., blackness cannot become non-blackness).
This shows essence is self-identical and cannot be contingent.
3
Study the second proof
The second proof argues that what depends on a cause is possible, and possibility is a relative state between essence and an attribute. For example, blackness can exist, not 'blackness can be blackness'. Thus, what requires a cause is possibility, not essence itself.
The passage ends mid-sentence here, so the proof is incomplete.
4
Reflect on incompleteness
Notice that the passage only covers the first division. The remaining three divisions (showing the dependent cannot be existence, nor the combination, and establishing the true dependent) are not provided.
This is a fragment from a longer argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الخامسة : المفتقر إلى المؤثر يمتنع [ أن يكون ] (٣) هو الماهية ، 1 ويمتنع أن يكون هو الوجود] (٣) ويمتنع أن يكون هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود ، وإذا امتنعت الأقسام الثلاثة ، امتنع كون الماهية مفتقرة إلى المؤثر . فيفتقر في تقرير هذا الكلام إلى إثبات أقسام (4) أربعة : الأول : قولنا : إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفتقر إلى المؤثر هو الماهية . وبيانه من وجهين :
الأول : إن كل ما [ كان بالغير، فإنه يجب أن يرتفع عند ارتفاع عدم ذلك الغير . فلو كانت الماهية من حيث هي هي، مفتقرة إلى المؤثر ، لزم من فرض عدم ذلك الغير (٥) ] بطلان الماهية ، من حيث هي هي [ لكن بطلان الماهية من حيث هي هي] (١) محال . لأن السواد يمتنع أن ينقلب غير سواد ، والبياض يمتنع أن ينقلب غير بياض .
والوجه الثاني : إن المفتقر إلى المؤثر ما يكون ممكنا ، والإمكان حالة نسبة إضافية بين الماهية وبين صفة من صفاتها ، لأنا إذا قلنا : إن كذا ممكن أن يكون كذا ، فهذا المعنى إنما يعقل إذا كان المفهوم من الموضوع مغايراً للمحمول . فإنه أن يقال : السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً . أما ما لا يمتنع أن يقال : السواد يمكن أن يكون موجوداً . فثبت أن المحوج إلى المؤثر [ هو الإمكان ، وثبت : أن يمتنع
The fifth objection: That which is dependent upon the effector cannot [be] the essence, and cannot be the existence, and cannot be the being-described of the essence by existence. If the three divisions are impossible, then the essence being dependent upon the effector is impossible. So in presenting this statement, it is necessary to establish four divisions: The first: our saying that it is impossible for that which is dependent upon the effector to be the essence. Its explanation is from two aspects: The first: Everything [that is by another, then it must cease when the non-existence of that other ceases. So if the essence considered in itself were dependent upon the effector, then from the supposition of the non-existence of that other] the falsity of the essence considered in itself would follow, [but the falsity of the essence considered in itself] is impossible, because blackness cannot turn into non-blackness, and whiteness cannot turn into non-whiteness. The second aspect: That which is dependent upon the effector is what is possible, and possibility is a relative state between the essence and one of its attributes. For when we say: 'Such-and-such can be such-and-such', this meaning is only understood if the concept of the subject is different from the predicate. For example, it is said: 'Blackness can be blackness'. But it is not impossible to say: 'Blackness can exist'. So it is established that that which necessitates the need for the effector [is possibility, and it is established that it is impossible]
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth objection (shubha) against the claim that things need a cause. The objection states that the entity which is dependent on the cause cannot be the essence (mahiyya), nor existence (wujud), nor the being-described of essence by existence (mawsufiyya al-mahiyya bi al-wujud). If all three are impossible, then the claim that an essence is dependent on a cause is false. The author then begins to establish the first division (that the dependent cannot be the essence) with two proofs. The first proof: Anything that exists through another must cease when that other is removed. If the essence were dependent on the cause, then the absence of the cause would entail the non-existence of the essence itself. But the essence as such cannot cease to be what it is (e.g., blackness cannot become non-blackness). Therefore, the essence cannot be dependent on the cause. The second proof: That which depends on a cause is what is possible (mumkin). Possibility is a relative state between the essence and one of its attributes. When we say 'something can be such', the subject and predicate are distinct. For blackness, we say it can exist, not that it can be blackness (since that is identical). Thus, what requires a cause is possibility, and it is established that it is impossible—but the text ends here, leaving the objection incomplete. The passage only covers the first division; the remaining three divisions are not provided in this window.

Key Terms
المفتقر
الماهية
الوجود
موصوفية
الإمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the essence itself, such as blackness, needs a cause to exist because it is not self-sufficient.
Correction: Razi argues that the essence considered in itself cannot be dependent because it cannot cease to be what it is; the need for a cause pertains to possibility, not to essence per se.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof given to show that the dependent entity cannot be the essence?
A) The essence is eternal.
B) The essence cannot cease to be what it is even if its cause is removed.
C) The essence is identical to existence.
D) The essence has no attributes.

Key Takeaway
The essence itself cannot be the dependent entity because it is self-identical and cannot cease to be itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi argues that your essence (who you are at your core) cannot be what depends on Allah for existence. If that is true, then what part of you truly relies on Him every moment? Are you living as if your possibility—your very being-possible—is the only thing that keeps you from nothing?
?
The first proof says that if something depends on another, it must cease when that other disappears. Consider your faith: if the people, habits, or comforts you rely on were taken away, would your trust in Allah still stand? Or is your faith itself dependent on those things?
?
Razi distinguishes between essence and possibility. In your daily life, do you tend to see yourself as a fixed 'good Muslim' (essence) or as a constant possibility that Allah actualizes? How does this shift in perspective affect your gratitude and reliance on Him today?

The Fifth Doubt: First Proof that Quiddity is Not Dependent
Sanusi states the three divisions and gives the first proof for the first division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure of the fifth doubt and the first proof that quiddity as such cannot be dependent because it cannot cease to be itself.

Core Idea
Quiddity as such cannot depend on a cause because it cannot be annihilated.

The fifth doubt of the skeptics attempts to show that nothing in creation is truly dependent on a cause. Sanusi first states the three possibilities for what could be dependent, then begins refuting each. In this lesson, we examine the first proof: if quiddity itself were dependent, removing the cause would destroy the quiddity—but quiddity is immutable.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt and the first proof
Read the opening statement where Sanusi lists three impossible possibilities, then the first proof's reasoning.
Notice that the proof uses a conditional: if dependent, then removal of cause leads to nullification.
2
Understand the first proof's logic
Grasp the principle: anything dependent on another must cease if that other is removed. Apply it to quiddity as such.
3
Reflect on the example
Sanusi gives examples of blackness and whiteness to show quiddity cannot turn into something else.
The quiddity of blackness is eternally blackness; it cannot become non-blackness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الخامسة : المفتقر إلى المؤثر يمتنع أن يكون هو الماهية، ويمتنع أن يكون هو الوجود، ويمتنع أن يكون هو موصوفية الماهية بالوجود، وإذا امتنعت الأقسام الثلاثة، امتنع كون الماهية مفتقرة إلى المؤثر. فيفتقر في تقرير هذا الكلام إلى إثبات أقسام أربعة: الأول: قولنا: إنه يمتنع أن يكون المفتقر إلى المؤثر هو الماهية. وبيانه من وجهين: الأول: إن كل ما كان بالغير، فإنه يجب أن يرتفع عند ارتفاع عدم ذلك الغير. فلو كانت الماهية من حيث هي هي، مفتقرة إلى المؤثر، لزم من فرض عدم ذلك الغير بطلان الماهية، من حيث هي هي، لكن بطلان الماهية من حيث هي هي محال. لأن السواد يمتنع أن ينقلب غير سواد، والبياض يمتنع أن ينقلب غير بياض. والوجه الثاني: إن المفتقر إلى المؤثر ما يكون ممكنا، والإمكان حالة نسبة إضافية بين الماهية وبين صفة من صفاتها، لأنا إذا قلنا: إن كذا ممكن أن يكون كذا، فهذا المعنى إنما يعقل إذا كان المفهوم من الموضوع مغايراً للمحمول. فإنه لا يقال: السواد يمكن أن يكون سواداً. أما ما لا يمتنع أن يقال: السواد يمكن أن يكون موجوداً. فثبت أن المحوج إلى المؤثر هو الإمكان، وثبت أن الإمكان حال نسبية، وثبت في بديهة العقل: أن الشيء الواحد من حيث إنه هو فقط، فإنه لا يعرض له شيء من الأحوال النسبية الإضافية، فيثبت: أن الإمكان يمتنع كونه عارضاً للحقيقة من حيث هي هي، وإذا كان المقتضى للحاجة ليس إلا الإمكان، وثبت أن الماهية من حيث هي هي يمتنع أن يعرض لها الإمكان ثبت أن الماهية من حيث هي هي يمتنع كونها محتاجة إلى المؤثر.
The fifth doubt: The dependent on the effect cannot be the quiddity, and cannot be existence, and cannot be the qualification of quiddity by existence. And if the three divisions are impossible, then the quiddity being dependent on the effect is impossible. So in stating this speech, it requires proving four sections. The first: our statement: that it is impossible for the dependent on the effect to be the quiddity. Its clarification is from two aspects: The first: Everything that is by another must cease when the non-existence of that other ceases. So if the quiddity, as such, were dependent on the effect, then from the assumption of the non-existence of that other, the nullification of the quiddity, as such, would follow. But nullification of the quiddity, as such, is impossible. Because blackness cannot turn into non-blackness, and whiteness cannot turn into non-whiteness. The second aspect: The dependent on the effect is what is possible (mumkin), and possibility (imkan) is a relative relational state between the quiddity and one of its attributes. For when we say: 'Such a thing is possible to be such,' this meaning is only intelligible if the concept of the subject is different from the predicate. For it is not said: 'Blackness can be blackness.' As for what is not impossible to say: 'Blackness can exist.' So it is established that the cause of need for the effect is possibility, and it is established that possibility is a relational state, and it is established in the intuition of reason that a single thing, as it is itself only, is not subject to any relative relational states. So it is established that possibility cannot be an accident of the essence as such. And since the requisite for need is nothing but possibility, and it is established that the quiddity as such cannot have possibility, it is established that the quiddity as such cannot be in need of the effect.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the fifth doubt, which claims that the dependent on the effect cannot be the quiddity, existence, or their relation, concluding that nothing is dependent. The author first states the doubt and then begins refuting the first division: that the quiddity is the dependent. He gives two proofs. The first proof: If the quiddity as such were dependent on an effect (i.e., a cause), then if that cause were removed, the quiddity itself would cease to exist. But the quiddity of a thing (e.g., blackness) cannot cease to be itself; it is essentially what it is. Therefore the quiddity as such cannot be dependent. The second proof: The real need for a cause is due to possibility (imkan), which is a relational attribute between a quiddity and its existence. But possibility cannot attach to the quiddity as such, because a single thing in itself has no relational states. Therefore the quiddity as such is not the subject of possibility, and thus not the thing that needs a cause. The author concludes that the quiddity as such cannot be in need of the effect.

Key Terms
الماهية
المفتقر إلى المؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think quiddity itself is contingent and dependent on a cause.
Correction: The first proof shows quiddity as such cannot be dependent because it cannot be annihilated.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, if the quiddity as such were dependent on the effect, what would follow from assuming the non-existence of that effect?
A) The quiddity would still exist as itself.
B) The quiddity would be nullified as such.
C) The quiddity would become another quiddity.
D) The quiddity would become necessary.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows quiddity as such cannot be dependent because it would be destroyed if its cause were removed, but quiddity is immutable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If quiddity as such cannot be dependent, and your existence is merely an accident of your essence, what does that say about the source of your identity? Are you defined by what you are or by the One who gives you existence? How does this affect your reliance on God?
?
Sanusi argues that blackness cannot become non-blackness. Think of a deeply ingrained flaw in your character that you have resigned yourself to. Could it be that you have mistaken a changeable attribute for an unchangeable essence? How might this reasoning empower you to seek transformation?
?
The proof shows that quiddity is not dependent. If your 'self' is a quiddity, then in what sense are you reliant on Allah? Does this make you independent? How does the Ash'ari understanding of occasionalism reconcile with this proof? Examine your heart: do you truly believe that every moment of your existence is sustained by Allah, or do you unconsciously assume your essence carries its own existence?

The Fifth Doubt: Second Proof that Quiddity is Not Dependent
Sanusi gives the second proof that the dependent cannot be quiddity, using the concept of possibility and its relational nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof that quiddity cannot be the dependent because need for a cause is due to possibility, which is a relational attribute that cannot attach to quiddity as such.

Core Idea
Need for a cause arises from possibility, but possibility is a relational state that cannot apply to quiddity itself.

In the previous lesson, we saw that quiddity cannot be dependent because it would be annihilated by removal of the cause. Now Sanusi presents a deeper argument: the real cause of need for a cause is possibility (imkan), and possibility is a relational attribute between quiddity and existence. But a simple essence like quiddity, considered in itself, cannot have relational attributes. Therefore quiddity itself is not the subject of possibility, and thus not the dependent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of possibility (imkan)
Learn that the need for a cause is due to possibility, which is a relational state between quiddity and its attributes.
Possibility is not an inherent property of quiddity alone.
2
Grasp the relational nature of possibility
Sanusi explains that possibility is a relative state (hal nisbi) only intelligible when subject and predicate differ.
Example: 'Blackness can exist' has a subject (blackness) and a different predicate (existence).
3
Apply the principle of a single thing having no relational states
A thing considered in itself has no relational attributes. Therefore possibility cannot attach to quiddity as such.
Thus quiddity as such does not have possibility and therefore does not need a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often attribute your successes or failures to causes you can see—effort, luck, circumstances. But if quiddity itself has no need for a cause, what does that mean for your assumption that the world runs on self-contained causes? Will you allow this to unsettle your reliance on secondary causes and redirect your trust to the First Cause alone?
?
The passage argues that a 'single thing as it is itself only' cannot have relational states. Consider your own identity: how often do you define yourself through relations—your job, your relationships, your achievements? Can you see yourself stripped of all those relations? If that stripped self cannot even be 'possible' on its own, how can it be the ground of your worth?
?
Sanusi says possibility is a relation between quiddity and an attribute like existence. Your own existence is not something you own; it is a relation to the Creator. Does your daily awareness reflect this dependency, or do you live as if existence is your intrinsic property? What concrete change would it take for you to live each moment as a relation to the One who gives existence?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
